Executive Summary

  • Engine Stability Crisis: V1 engine crashes, deadlocks, and EngineDeadError failures are blocking the Model Runner V2 default rollout milestone and threatening production reliability.
  • Frontier Model Breakage: Critical day-0 failures across Gemma 4, DeepSeek V3.2, and Qwen3.5 violate the roadmap's commitment to frontier model support and damage enterprise confidence.
  • Blackwell Compatibility Gap: Missing RTX 50-series support spans installation, large-scale serving, and quantization SIGs, blocking adoption of NVIDIA's latest consumer and enterprise hardware.
  • Tool Calling Regression: Gemma 4 parser corruption and widespread structured output failures create critical user-facing regressions that compromise production AI application reliability.
  • Performance Degradation: Significant throughput regressions on flagship models like Qwen3.5-397B (-19%) and Gemma 4 (~90% slowdown) undermine vLLM's performance leadership positioning.
  • Quantization Instability: FP8/NVFP4 quantization producing garbage output across MoE architectures threatens cost-efficiency gains and enterprise deployment viability.
▾

#1 Core Engine

75 issues 18 clusters

System crashes, deadlocks, and EngineDeadError issues directly block the critical Model Runner V2 default rollout milestone and affect fundamental engine stability.

[RFC]: Dynamic Speculation Length (DSL) with Confidence-Threshold Early Exit for vLLM Speculative Decoding
### Motivation. Standard speculative decoding always runs the draft model for exactly `num_speculative_tokens` steps per decode iteration. When the draft model is uncertain early in the speculation chain, every additional step wastes compute: the low-confidence tokens are almost certainly rejected by the target model, and the draft forward passes are lost work. Setting `num_speculative_tokens` conservatively (e.g., 5) leaves throughput on the table during high-confidence sequences. Setting it...

11 Add support for advanced quantization methods: TurboQuant, RotorQuant, ParoQuant for KV cache compression #38291 Add Rotorquant support
[Feature]: Add Rotorquant support
### 🚀 The feature, motivation and pitch **RotorQuant** is a Clifford algebra-based reimagining of TurboQuant (ICLR 2026) for KV cache compression. It replaces the dense d×d random orthogonal rotation matrix used in TurboQuant with lightweight Clifford rotors from Cl(3,0), achieving **10–19× faster** quantization on NVIDIA GPUs, **9–31× faster** on Apple Silicon, and using **44× fewer parameters** — all while matching TurboQuant's attention fidelity on real models. - **Paper/Report:** https://w...

12 Implement vLLM IR functional representation for custom operations compilation #38744 Automatically compile native impl for IR ops
[RFC][vLLM IR]: Automatically compile native impl for IR ops
### Motivation. Sometimes we need to call an IR op inside another opaque torch custom op. That means the IR op will be invisible to model-level compilation, and dispatching to the raw native implementation will hurt performance. This problem is not unique to vLLM IR; it happens for `CustomOp` instances as well, and we currently circumvent it by wrapping `forward_native` with `torch.compile`. Prime examples of this are `SiluAndMul` and `QuantFP8` inside `fused_moe`. The same mechanism is utiliz...

15 Disable sequence parallelism for piecewise compilation due to tensor passing issues #35771 Disable Sequence Parallelism (SP) for piecewise compilation
[RFC][torch.compile]: Disable Sequence Parallelism (SP) for piecewise compilation
### Motivation. When compiling piecewise (dynamo partition and non-empty `splitting_ops`), the RMSNorm residual tensor gets passed between piecewise subgraphs. This poses a challenge for sequence parallelism as it splits along the num_tokens dimension, which means the residual gets split across TP ranks. That means the size of the residual is different before and after the SP pass. The initial implementation of SP had to work on piecewise compiled graphs as it was done before we had full cudag...

#20402 vLLM-compile warm-start time should be close to zero
[RFC]: vLLM-compile (minus cudagraphs) warm-start time should be close to zero
### Motivation. @BoyuanFeng did some benchmarks of vLLM cold vs warm start of a 70B model. In the warm start, compilation (ignoring cudagraphs) took 25 out of 132 seconds, almost 20% of the time. On warm start, all of the hard work (compiling artifacts) should have been already done. The theoretical minimum amount of time that vLLM-compile needs to spend in warm start is the amount of time it takes to load all the compiled code. ![Image](https://github.com/user-attachments/assets/b34204f8-5ad...
